standardsmany governmental standard and regulation relating to safety fuel economy emission control noise control vehicle recycling substance of concern vehicle damage and theft prevention are applicable to new motor vehicle engine and equipment in addition manufacturing and other automotive assembly facility are subject to stringent standard regulating air emission water discharge and the handling and disposal of hazardous substance the most significant of the standard and regulation affecting are discussed below vehicle emission controlu requirement federal and california tailpipe emission standard the environmental protection agency epa and the california air resource board carb have established motor vehicle tailpipe and evaporative emission standard that become increasingly stringent over time seventeen state have adopted california light duty standard four state have adopted california heavy duty standard and other state are expected to join both federal and california regulation also require motor vehicle to be equipped with on board diagnostic obd system that monitor emission related system and component in addition light and medium duty vehicle and heavy duty engine must be certified by epa prior to sale in the united state and by carb prior to sale in california and the relevant state canada accepts epa certification compliance with emission standard obd requirement and related regulation can be challenging and can drive increased product development cost warranty cost and vehicle recall carb ha adopted new emission regulation applicable to model year heavy duty engine well extended heavy duty warranty requirement beginning with the model year and epa ha proposed stringent heavy duty standard beginning with the model year these rule include more stringent emission standard well new requirement affecting durability testing warranty and obd carb ha also adopted new light duty emission standard applicable to model year vehicle including more stringent emission standard and other new emission requirement these new rule are expected to impose increased challenge and cost on the development of light duty vehicle and heavy duty engine compliance with automobile emission standard depends in part on the widespread availability of high quality and consistent automotive fuel that the vehicle were designed to use legislative regulatory and judicial development related to fuel quality at both the national and state level could affect vehicle manufacturer warranty cost well their ability to comply with vehicle emission standard business continued the california vehicle emission program also includes requirement for manufacturer to produce and deliver for sale zero emission vehicle zevs california light duty vehicle zev regulation which us system based on credit that can be banked and carried forward mandate annual increase in the production and sale of battery electric fuel cell and plug in hybrid vehicle for model year this regulation will require approximately of manufacturer california light duty vehicle sale volume be zevs in august california approved sweeping revision to the zev regulation beginning with the model year the revised zev rule mandate zev sale requirement rising to by the revised regulation also imposes significant restriction on credit usage and new requirement for ev battery durability california ha also instituted zev regulation governing medium and heavy duty vehicle beginning with the model year these stringent zev requirement covering light medium and heavy duty vehicle could entail significant cost and compliance challenge and include complex warranty and recall requirement compliance with zev rule depends on market condition including the pace of adoption of ev technology readiness and battery raw material availability well the availability of adequate infrastructure to support vehicle charging european requirement european union eu and regulation directive and related legislation limit the amount of regulated pollutant that may be emitted by new motor vehicle and engine sold in the eu and the united kingdom regulatory stringency ha increased significantly with the application of stage vi emission standard first introduced in and the implementation of laboratory test cycle for and emission and the introduction of on road emission testing using portable emission analyzer real driving emission or rde these on road emission test are in addition to the laboratory based test first introduced in the divergence the regulatory limit that is tested in laboratory condition and the allowed value measured in rde test will ultimately be reduced to zero the regulatory demand increase in addition new requirement for tailpipe and non tailpipe emission will be included in the upcoming euro regulation and the lead time for engineering and type approval may potentially be short the cost associated with complying with all of these requirement are significant and following the eu commission indication of it intent to accelerate emission rule in it road map publication eu green deal well the eu sustainable mobility action plan these challenge will continue in european market including the united kingdom in addition the whole vehicle type approval wvta regulation ha been updated to increase the stringency of in market surveillance moreover following the withdrawal from the european union we may be subject to diverging requirement in our european market which could increase vehicle complexity and duty there is an increasing trend of city access restriction for internal combustion engine powered vehicle the access rule introduced are developed by individual city based on their specific concern resulting in rapid deployment of access rule that differ greatly among city the speed of implementation of access rule may directly influence customer vehicle residual value and choice of next purchase in an effort to support the paris accord some country are adopting yearly increase in tax where such system is in place and publishing date by when internal combustion powered vehicle may no longer be registered norway in and the united kingdom and the netherlands in other national requirement many country in an effort to address air quality and climate change concern are adopting previous version of european or united nation economic commission for europe un ece mobile source emission regulation some country have adopted more advanced regulation based on the most recent version of european or regulation for example the china stage vi light duty vehicle emission standard based on european stage vi emission standard for light duty vehicle evaporative and refueling emission standard and carb obd ii requirement incorporate two level of stringency for tailpipe emission under the level one vi standard which is currently in place nationwide in china the emission limit are comparable to the eu stage vi limit except for carbon monoxide which is lower than the eu stage vi limit the more stringent level two vi standard emission limit are approximately lower than the eu stage vi limit depending on the pollutant while level two vi is not slated for nationwide implementation july the government ha encouraged the more economically developed city and province to pull ahead implementation for example beijing shanghai tianjin hebei province and guangdong province have all begun implementing level two vi both china stage vii light duty vehicle and heavy duty vehicle emission regulation are currently under pre study and the ministry of ecology and environment ha advised that the stage vii regulation will have more stringent limit on pollutant emission and will establish limit for greenhouse gas primarily tailpipe emission in south america most country are evolving to implement more stringent requirement accepting europe and regulation except brazil which ha unique local process called proconve based on regulation for light duty vehicle and european regulation for heavy duty vehicle business continued canadian criterion emission regulation are largely aligned with requirement however the existing zev regulation in quebec and those published in british columbia in july are more stringent than those in place in california both british columbia and quebec have proposed draft amendment to their regulation to increase requirement starting in and respectively the federal government ha published draft light duty zev sale requirement through an amendment to the passenger automobile and light truck greenhouse gas emission regulation and ha also published it intent to develop zev sale requirement for heavy duty vehicle other province have signaled their interest in light duty zev sale regulation but are awaiting the finalization of the federal zev regulation elsewhere there is mix of regulation and process based on and eu standard not all country have adopted appropriate fuel quality standard to accompany the stringent emission standard adopted this could lead to compliance problem particularly if obd or in use surveillance requirement are implemented global development in recent year epa and carb have increased their focus on the use of defeat device defeat device are element of design typically embedded in software that improperly cause the emission control system to function le effectively during normal on road driving than during an official laboratory emission test without justification are prohibited by law in many jurisdiction and we do not use defeat device in our vehicle regulator around the world continue to scrutinize automaker emission testing which ha led to number of defeat device settlement by various manufacturer epa is carrying additional non standard test part of it vehicle certification program carb ha also been conducting extensive non standard emission test which in some case have resulted in certification delay for diesel vehicle in the past several european country have conducted non standard emission test and published the result and in some case this supplemental testing ha triggered investigation of manufacturer for possible defeat device testing is expected to continue on an ongoing basis in addition plaintiff attorney are pursuing consumer class action lawsuit based on alleged excessive emission from car and truck which could in turn prompt further investigation by regulator vehicle fuel economy and greenhouse gas standardsu requirement light duty vehicle federal law requires that light duty vehicle meet minimum corporate average fuel economy cafe standard set by the national highway traffic safety administration nhtsa manufacturer are subject to substantial civil penalty if they fail to meet the cafe standard in any model year after taking into account all available credit for the preceding five model year and expected credit for the three succeeding model year the law requires nhtsa to promulgate and enforce separate cafe standard applicable to each manufacturer fleet of domestic passenger car imported passenger car and light duty truck epa also regulates vehicle greenhouse gas ghg emission under the clean air act the vast majority of ghgs emitted by vehicle are the result of fuel combustion ghg emission standard are similar to fuel economy standard thus nhtsa and epa coordinate with each other on their fuel economy and ghg standard respectively to avoid potential inconsistency beginning with the model year epa and nhtsa jointly promulgated harmonized ghg and fuel economy regulation under came to be known the one national program onp framework california which had promulgated it own state specific set of ghg regulation agreed that compliance with the federal program would satisfy compliance with it own ghg requirement thereby avoiding patchwork of potentially conflicting federal and state ghg standard onp ha required manufacturer to achieve increasingly stringent year over year standard onp wa envisioned to continue at least through the model year in epa introduced significantly le stringent fuel economy and ghg standard applicable to model year the federal government also revoked california authority to set and enforce it own vehicle ghg standard well the authority of other state that opted in to california standard california continued to assert it authority to regulate vehicle ghgs challenged in court the federal government preemption action withdrew from onp and planned to return to enforcing it own state specific ghg standard business continued the litigation over both standard and preemption with uncertain outcome created difficulty for purpose of ford future product planning to avoid bifurcated regulatory scenario in which california and the other state that adopted california ghg standard enforce one set of rule while different set of rule applies in the rest of the country ford reached an agreement with california on set of term for an alternative framework in which ford committed to meet designated set of standard on national basis in lieu of the california regulatory program this framework enabled ford to continue it product planning on nationwide basis while being consistent with ford environmental goal ford finalized it agreement with california in and other state that adopted the california standard indicated they would respect the agreement in epa evaluated the stringency of light duty fuel economy and ghg standard through the model year and considered whether to restore the stringency to the previous onp level or greater epa finalized this evaluation in december establishing ghg standard applicable to model year with stringency that exceeded onp suit because many previously targeted company have filed for bankruptcy or emerged from bankruptcy relieved of liability for such claim most of the asbestos litigation we face involves individual who claim to have worked on the brake of our vehicle we are prepared to defend these case and believe that the scientific evidence confirms our long standing position that there is no increased risk of asbestos related disease result of exposure to the type of asbestos formerly used in the brake on our vehicle the extent of our financial exposure to asbestos litigation remains very difficult to estimate and could include both compensatory and punitive damage award the majority of our asbestos case do not specify dollar amount for damage in many of the other case the dollar amount specified is the jurisdictional minimum and the vast majority of these case involve multiple defendant some of these case may also involve multiple plaintiff and we may be unable to tell from the pleading which plaintiff are making claim against opposed to other defendant annual payout and defense cost may become significant in the future our accrual for asbestos matter includes probable loss for both asserted and unasserted claim consumer matterswe provide warranty on the vehicle we sell warranty are offered for specific period of time and or mileage and vary depending upon the type of product and the geographic location of it sale pursuant to these warranty we will repair replace or adjust part on vehicle that are defective in factory supplied material or workmanship during the specified warranty period we are defendant in numerous action in state and federal court alleging breach of warranty and claiming damage based on state and federal consumer protection law remedy under these statute may include vehicle repurchase civil penalty and payment by ford of the plaintiff attorney fee in some case plaintiff also include an allegation of fraud remedy for fraud claim may include contract rescission vehicle repurchase and punitive damage the cost of these litigation matter is included in our warranty cost we accrue obligation for warranty cost at the time of sale using patterned estimation model that includes historical information regarding the nature frequency and average cost of claim for each vehicle line by model year we reevaluate the adequacy of our accrual factor affecting ford and the automotive industrycovid and supplier disruption the impact of covid including change in consumer behavior pandemic fear and market downturn and restriction on business and individual activity ha created significant volatility in the global economy outbreak in certain region continue to cause intermittent covid related disruption in our supply chain and local manufacturing operation we also continue to face supplier disruption due to labor shortage and other production issue in addition to the continuing semiconductor shortage our inconsistent production schedule ha been disruptive to our supplier operation which in turn ha led to higher cost and production shortfall further action taken by russia in ukraine have impacted and could further impact our supplier particularly our lower tier supplier well our operation in europe for additional information on the impact of supplier disruption see the outlook section on page currency exchange rate volatility after aggressively easing monetary policy in response to the covid pandemic the federal reserve and other central bank around the world in began to withdraw monetary stimulus by raising interest rate period of monetary policy tightening are often associated with heightened financial market and currency volatility especially for those market that are outlier in term of their economic or monetary policy backdrop this is notable for many emerging market which may also face increased exposure to commodity price and political instability contributing to unpredictable movement in the value of their exchange rate in addition to direct impact on the financial flow of global automotive company currency movement can also impact pricing of vehicle exported to overseas market in most market exchange rate are market determined and all are impacted by many different macroeconomic and policy factor and thus likely to remain volatile however in some market exchange rate are heavily influenced or controlled by government pricing pressure over the last year price of both new and used vehicle have increased substantially due to strong demand supply shortage and inflationary cost we have already observed some moderation in the rate of price increase auto production slowly recovers from the semiconductor shortage but it is unclear whether price will decline fully to pre covid pandemic level over the long term intense competition and excess capacity are likely to put downward pressure on inflation adjusted price for similarly contented vehicle and contribute to challenging pricing environment for the automotive industry in most major market commodity and energy price price for commodity remain volatile in some case spot price for various commodity have recently diverged somewhat anticipated weakening in global industrial activity mitigates price increase for base metal such steel and aluminum while precious metal palladium and raw material that are used in battery for electric vehicle lithium cobalt nickel graphite and manganese among other material for battery remain high the net impact on and our supplier ha been higher material cost overall to help ensure supply of raw material for critical component battery we like others in the industry have entered into multi year sourcing agreement and may enter into additional agreement similar dynamic are impacting energy market with europe particularly exposed to the risk of both higher price and constraint on supply of natural gas due to the ongoing conflict in ukraine such shortage may impact facility operated by or our supplier which could have an impact on in europe and other region in the long term the outcome of de carbonization and electrification of the vehicle fleet may depress oil demand but the global energy transition will also contribute to ongoing volatility of oil and other energy price for additional information on commodity cost see the outlook section on page vehicle profitability our financial result depend on the profitability of the vehicle we sell which may vary significantly by vehicle line in general larger vehicle tend to command higher price and be more profitable than smaller vehicle both across and within vehicle segment for example in north america our larger more profitable vehicle had an average contribution margin that wa of our total average contribution margin across all vehicle whereas our smaller vehicle had significantly lower contribution margin in addition government regulation aimed at reducing emission and increasing fuel efficiency zev mandate and low emission zone and other factor that accelerate the transition to electrified vehicle may increase the cost of vehicle by more than the perceived benefit to consumer and dampen margin management discussion and analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued trade policy to the extent government in various region implement or intensify barrier to continue to see near term impact on our business due to inflation including ongoing global price pressure in the wake of russia invasion of ukraine driving up energy price freight premium and other operating cost above normal rate although headline inflation in the united state and europe appears to have peaked gasoline and natural gas price recede from the latest spike core inflation excluding food and energy price remains elevated and is source of continued cost pressure on business and household interest rate have increased significantly central bank in developed country attempt to subdue inflation while government deficit and debt remain at high level in many global market accordingly the eventual implication of higher government deficit and debt tighter monetary policy and potentially higher long term interest rate may drive higher cost of capital for the business at ford credit rising interest rate may impact it ability to source funding and offer financing at competitive rate which could reduce it financing margin revenueour automotive segment revenue is generated primarily by sale of vehicle part and accessory revenue is recorded when control is transferred to our customer generally our dealer and distributor for the majority of sale this occurs when product are shipped from our manufacturing facility however we defer portion of the consideration received when there is separate future or stand ready performance obligation such extended service contract or ongoing vehicle connectivity revenue related to extended service contract is recognized over the term of the agreement in proportion to the cost we expect to incur in satisfying the contract obligation revenue related to other future or stand ready performance obligation is generally recognized on straight line basis over the period in which service are expected to be performed vehicle sold to daily rental car company with an obligation to repurchase for guaranteed amount exercisable at the option of the customer are accounted for operating lease with lease revenue recognized over the term of the lease proceeds from the sale of vehicle at auction are recognized in revenue upon transfer of control of the vehicle to the buyer most of the vehicle sold by to our dealer and distributor are financed at wholesale by ford credit upon ford credit originating the wholesale receivable related to dealer purchase of vehicle ford credit pay cash to the relevant automotive legal entity in payment of the dealer obligation for the purchase price of the vehicle the dealer pay the wholesale finance receivable to ford credit when it sell the vehicle to retail customer our ford credit segment revenue is generated primarily from interest on finance receivables and revenue from operating lease revenue from interest on finance receivables is recognized over the term of the receivable using the interest method and includes the amortization of certain deferred origination cost revenue from operating lease is recognized on straight line basis over the term of the lease transaction between our automotive and ford credit segment occur in the ordinary course of business for example we offer special retail financing and lease incentive to dealer customer who choose to finance or lease our vehicle from ford credit the cost for these incentive is included in our estimate of variable consideration at the date the related vehicle sale to our dealer are recorded in order to compensate ford credit for the lower interest or lease payment offered to the retail customer we pay the discounted value of the incentive directly to ford credit when it originates the retail finance or lease contract with the dealer customer ford credit recognizes the incentive amount over the life of retail finance contract an element of financing revenue and over the life of lease contract reduction to depreciation see note of the note to the financial statement for more detailed discussion of transaction between our automotive and ford credit segment management discussion and analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued cost and expensesour income statement classifies our company excluding ford credit total cost and expense into two category cost of sale and ii selling administrative and other expense we include within cost of sale those cost related to the development production and distribution of our vehicle part accessory and service specifically we include in cost of sale each of the following material cost including commodity cost freight cost warranty including product recall cost labor and other cost related to the development and production of our vehicle and connectivity part accessory and service depreciation and amortization and other associated cost we include within selling administrative and other expense labor and other cost not directly related to the development and production of our vehicle part accessory and service including such expense advertising and sale promotion cost certain of our cost such material cost generally vary directly with change in volume and mix of production in our industry production volume often varies significantly from quarter to quarter and year to year quarterly production volume experience seasonal shift throughout the year including peak retail sale season and the impact on production of model changeover and new product launch annual production volume are heavily impacted by external economic factor including the pace of economic growth and factor such the availability of consumer credit and cost of fuel result we analyze the profit impact of certain cost change holding constant present year volume and mix and currency exchange in order to evaluate our cost trend absent the impact of varying production and currency exchange level we analyze these cost change in the following category contribution cost these cost typically vary with production volume these cost include material including commodity warranty and freight and duty cost structural cost these cost typically do not have directly proportionate relationship to production volume these cost include manufacturing vehicle and software engineering spending related advertising and sale promotion administrative information technology and selling and pension and opeb cost while contribution cost generally vary directly in proportion to production volume element within our structural cost category are impacted to differing degree by change in production volume we also have varying degree of discretion when it come to controlling the different element within our structural cost for example depreciation and amortization expense largely is associated with prior capital spending decision on the other hand while labor cost do not vary directly with production volume manufacturing labor cost may be impacted by change in volume for example when we increase overtime add production shift or add personnel to support volume increase other structural cost such advertising or engineering cost do not necessarily have directly proportionate relationship to production volume our structural cost generally are within our discretion although to varying degree and can be adjusted over time in response to external factor we consider certain structural cost to be direct investment in future growth and revenue for example structural cost are necessary to grow our business and improve profitability invest in new product and technology respond to increasing industry sale volume and grow our market share cost of sale and selling administrative and other expense for full year were billion our automotive segment material and commodity cost make up the largest portion of these cost and expense followed by structural cost although material cost are our largest absolute cost our margin can be affected significantly by change in any category of cost analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued with respect to change in working capital in general we carry relatively low automotive segment trade receivables compared with our trade payable because the majority of our automotive wholesale are financed primarily by ford credit immediately upon the sale of vehicle to dealer which generally occurs shortly after being produced in contrast our automotive trade payable are based primarily on industry standard production supplier payment term of about day result our cash flow deteriorates if wholesale volume and the corresponding revenue decrease while trade payable continue to become due conversely our cash flow improves if wholesale volume and the corresponding revenue increase while new trade payable are generally not due for about day for example the suspension of production at most of our assembly plant and lower industry volume due to covid in early resulted in an initial deterioration of our cash flow while the subsequent resumption of manufacturing operation and return to pre covid production level at most of our assembly plant resulted in subsequent improvement of our cash flow even in normal economic condition however these working capital balance generally are subject to seasonal change that can impact cash flow for example we typically experience cash flow timing difference associated with inventory and payable due to our annual summer and december shutdown period when production and therefore inventory and wholesale volume are usually at their lowest level while payable continue to come due and be paid the net impact of this typically result in cash outflow from change in our working capital balance during these shutdown period our finished product inventory at december wa higher year over year due to production and release scheduling which resulted in higher sale inventory in transit inventory and unit awaiting upfit in response to or in anticipation of our inventory moreover in order to secure critical material for production of electric vehicle we have entered into and plan to continue to enter into offtake agreement with raw material supplier and estimateswe consider an accounting estimate to be critical if the accounting estimate requires to make assumption about matter that were highly uncertain at the time the accounting estimate wa made and change in the estimate that are reasonably likely to occur from period to period or use of different estimate that we reasonably could have used in the current period would have material impact on our financial condition or result of operation management ha discussed the development and selection of these critical accounting estimate with the audit committee of our board of director in addition there are other item within our financial statement that require estimation but are not deemed critical defined above change in estimate used in these and other item could have material impact on our financial statement warranty and field service actionsnature of estimate required we provide base warranty on the product we sell for specific period of time and or mileage which vary depending upon the type of product and the geographic location of it sale separately we also periodically perform field service action related to safety recall emission recall and other product campaign pursuant to these warranty and field service action we will repair replace or adjust part on vehicle that are defective in factory supplied material or workmanship we accrue the estimated cost of both base warranty coverage and field service action at the time of sale in addition from time to time we issue extended warranty at our expense the estimated cost of which is accrued at the time of issuance assumption and approach used we establish our estimate of base warranty obligation using patterned estimation model we use historical information regarding the nature frequency and average cost of claim for each vehicle line by model year we reevaluate our estimate of base warranty obligation on regular basis experience ha shown that initial data for any given model year may be volatile therefore our process relies on long term historical average until sufficient data are available with actual experience we use the data to update the historical average we then compare the resulting accrual with present spending rate to ass whether the balance are adequate to meet expected future obligation based on this data we update our estimate necessary field service action may occur in period beyond the base warranty coverage period we establish our estimate of field service action obligation using patterned estimation model we use historical information regarding the nature frequency severity and average cost of claim for each model year we ass our obligation for field service action on regular basis using actual claim experience and update our estimate necessary due to the uncertainty and potential volatility of the factor used in establishing our estimate change in our assumption could materially affect our financial condition and result of operation see note of the note to the financial statement for information regarding warranty and field service action cost pension and other postretirement employee benefit nature of estimate required the estimation of our defined benefit pension and opeb plan obligation and expense requires that we make use of estimate of the present value of the projected future payment to all participant taking into consideration the likelihood of potential future event such demographic experience and health care cost increase plan obligation and expense are based on existing retirement plan provision no assumption is made regarding any potential future change to benefit provision beyond those to which we are presently committed in existing labor contract management discussion and analysis of financial condition and payment are discounted at the rate on the curve to determine the year end obligation expected long term rate of return on plan asset our expected long term rate of return considers input from range of advisor for capital market return inflation bond yield and other variable adjusted for specific aspect of our investment strategy by plan historical return also are considered when appropriate the outlook and assumed inflation inflation our inflation assumption is based on an evaluation of external market indicator including real gross domestic product growth and central bank inflation target analysis of financial condition and result of operation continued assumption and approach used we are subject to the income tax law and regulation of the many jurisdiction in which we operate these tax law and regulation are complex and involve uncertainty in the application to our fact and circumstance that may be open to interpretation we recognize benefit for these uncertain tax position based upon process that requires judgment regarding the technical application of the law regulation and various related judicial opinion if in our judgment it is more likely than not defined likelihood of more than that the uncertain tax position will be settled favorably for we estimate an amount that ultimately will be realized this process is inherently subjective since it requires our assessment of the probability of future outcome we evaluate these uncertain tax position on quarterly basis including consideration of change in fact and circumstance such new regulation or recent judicial opinion well the status of audit activity by taxing authority change to our estimate of the amount to be realized are recorded in our provision for income tax during the period in which the change occurred we must also ass the likelihood that we will be able to recover our deferred tax asset against future source of taxable income and reduce the carrying amount of deferred tax asset by recording valuation allowance if based on all available evidence it is more likely than not that all or portion of such asset will not be realized this assessment which is completed on taxing jurisdiction basis take into account various type of evidence including the following nature frequency and severity of current and cumulative financial reporting loss pattern of objectively measured recent financial reporting loss is heavily weighted source of negative evidence we generally consider cumulative pre tax loss in the three year period ending with the current quarter to be significant negative evidence regarding future profitability we also consider the strength and trend of earnings well other relevant factor in certain circumstance historical information may not be relevant due to change in our business operation source of future taxable income future reversal of existing temporary difference are heavily weighted source of objectively verifiable positive evidence projection accounting standard see note of the note to the financial statement quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market riskoverviewwe are exposed to variety of market and other risk including the effect of change in foreign currency exchange rate commodity price and interest rate well risk to availability of funding source hazard event and specific asset risk these risk affect our automotive and ford credit segment differently we monitor and manage these exposure an integral part of our overall risk management program which includes regular report to central management committee the global risk management committee grmc the grmc is chaired by our chief financial officer and the committee includes our controller and treasurer our automotive and ford credit segment are exposed to liquidity risk including the possibility of having to curtail business or being unable to meet financial obligation they come due because funding source may be reduced or become unavailable our plan is to maintain funding source to ensure liquidity through variety of economic or business cycle discussed in greater detail in item our funding source include sale of receivables in securitizations and other structured financing unsecured debt issuance equity and equity linked issuance and bank borrowing we are exposed to variety of risk such loss or damage to property liability claim and employee injury we protect against these risk through the purchase of commercial insurance that is designed to protect above our self insured retention against event that could generate significant loss direct responsibility for the execution of our market risk management strategy resides with our treasurer office and is governed by written policy and procedure separation of duty is maintained between the development and authorization of derivative trade the transaction of derivative and the settlement of cash flow regular audit are conducted to ensure that appropriate control are in place and that they remain effective in addition our market risk exposure and our use of derivative to manage these exposure are approved by the grmc and reviewed by the audit committee of our board of director in accordance with our corporate risk management policy we use derivative instrument when available such forward contract swap and option that economically hedge certain exposure foreign currency commodity and interest rate we do not use derivative contract for trading market making or speculative purpose in certain instance we forgo hedge accounting and in certain other instance our derivative do not qualify for hedge accounting either situation result in unrealized gain and loss that are recognized in income for additional information on our derivative see note of the note to the financial statement the market and counterparty risk of our automotive and ford credit segment are discussed and quantified below automotive market riskour automotive segment frequently ha expenditure and receipt denominated in foreign currency including the following purchase and sale of finished vehicle and production part debt and other payable subsidiary dividend and investment in foreign operation these expenditure and receipt create exposure to change in exchange rate we also are exposed to change in price of commodity used in the production of our vehicle and change in interest rate foreign currency risk commodity risk and interest rate risk are measured and quantified using model to evaluate the sensitivity of market value to instantaneous parallel shift in rate and or price foreign currency risk foreign currency risk is the possibility that our financial result could be worse than planned because of change in currency exchange rate accordingly our practice is to use derivative instrument to hedge our economic exposure with respect to forecasted revenue and cost asset liability and firm commitment denominated in certain foreign currency consistent with our overall risk management strategy in our hedging action we use derivative instrument commonly used by corporation to reduce foreign exchange risk forward contract quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued the net fair value of foreign exchange forward contract including adjustment for credit risk of december wa an asset of million compared with liability of million of december the potential change in the fair value from change in the underlying exchange rate in dollar term would have been billion at december compared with billion at december the sensitivity analysis presented is hypothetical and assumes foreign exchange rate change are instantaneous and adverse across all currency in reality some of our exposure offset and foreign exchange rate move in different magnitude and at different time and any change in fair value would generally be offset by change in the underlying exposure see note of the note to the financial statement for more information regarding our foreign currency exchange contract commodity price risk commodity price risk is the possibility that our financial result could be worse than planned because of change in the price of commodity used in the production of motor vehicle such base metal steel copper and aluminum precious metal palladium energy natural gas and electricity and plastic resin polypropylene we transition to greater mix of electric vehicle we expect to increase our reliance on lithium cobalt nickel graphite and manganese among other material for battery accordingly our practice is to use derivative instrument to hedge the price risk with respect to forecasted purchase of certain commodity that we can economically hedge and consistent with our overall risk management strategy in our hedging action we use derivative instrument commonly used by corporation to reduce commodity price risk financially settled forward contract the extent to which we hedge is also impacted by our ability to achieve designated hedge accounting the net fair value of commodity forward contract including adjustment for credit risk of december wa liability of million compared with an asset of change in fair value would generally be offset by change in the underlying exposure in addition our purchasing organization with guidance from the grmc appropriate negotiates contract for the continuous supply of raw material in some case these contract stipulate minimum purchase amount and specific price and therefore play role in managing commodity price risk interest rate risk interest rate risk relates to the loss we could incur in our company cash investment portfolio due to change in interest rate our interest rate sensitivity analysis on the investment portfolio includes cash and cash equivalent and net marketable security at december company cash consisted of billion of rivian marketable security and billion of cash in our investment portfolio compared to billion of rivian marketable security and billion of cash in our investment portfolio at december we invest the portfolio in security of various type and maturity the value of which are subject to fluctuation in interest rate the investment strategy is based on clearly defined risk and liquidity guideline to maintain liquidity minimize risk and earn reasonable return on the short term investment in investing the cash in our investment portfolio safety of principal is the primary objective and risk adjusted return is the secondary objective at any time rise in interest rate could have material adverse impact on the fair value of our portfolio assuming hypothetical increase in interest rate of one percentage point the value of our portfolio would be reduced by million calculated of december this compare to million calculated of december while these are our best estimate of the impact of the specified interest rate scenario actual result could differ from those projected the sensitivity analysis presented assumes interest rate change are instantaneous parallel shift in the yield curve in reality interest rate change of this magnitude are rarely instantaneous or parallel quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued ford credit market riskmarket risk for ford credit is the possibility that change in interest and currency exchange rate will adversely affect cash flow and economic value interest rate risk generally ford credit asset and the related debt have different re pricing period and consequently respond differently to change in interest rate ford credit asset consist primarily of fixed rate retail financing and operating lease contract and floating rate wholesale receivables fixed rate retail financing and operating lease contract generally require customer to make equal monthly payment over the life of the contract wholesale receivables are originated to finance new and used vehicle held in dealer inventory and generally require dealer to pay floating rate debt consists primarily of short and long term unsecured and securitized debt ford credit term debt instrument are principally fixed rate and require fixed and equal interest payment over the life of the instrument and single principal payment at maturity ford credit interest rate risk management objective is to reduce volatility in it cash flow and volatility in it economic value from change in interest rate based on an established risk tolerance that may vary by market ford credit us economic value sensitivity analysis and re pricing gap analysis to evaluate potential long term effect of change in interest rate it then enters into interest rate swap to convert portion of it floating rate debt to fixed or it fixed rate debt to floating to ensure that ford credit exposure fall within the established tolerance ford credit also us pre tax cash flow sensitivity analysis to monitor the level of near term cash flow exposure the pre tax cash flow sensitivity analysis measure the change in expected cash flow associated with ford credit interest rate sensitive asset liability and derivative financial instrument from hypothetical change in interest rate over twelve month horizon interest rate swap are placed to maintain exposure within approved threshold and the asset liability committee review the re pricing mismatch monthly to provide quantitative measure of the sensitivity of it pre tax cash flow to change in interest rate ford credit us interest rate scenario that assume hypothetical instantaneous increase or decrease of one percentage point in all interest rate across all maturity parallel shift well base case that assumes that all interest rate remain constant at existing level in reality interest rate change are rarely instantaneous or parallel and rate could move more or le than the one percentage point assumed in ford credit analysis result the actual impact to pre tax cash flow could be higher or lower than the result detailed in the table below these interest rate scenario are purely hypothetical and do not represent ford credit view of future interest rate movement under these interest rate scenario ford credit expects more asset than debt and liability to re price in the next twelve month other thing being equal this mean that during period of rising interest rate the interest received on ford credit asset will increase more than the interest paid on ford credit debt thereby initially increasing ford credit pre tax cash flow during period of falling interest rate ford credit would expect it pre tax cash flow to initially decrease ford credit pre tax cash flow sensitivity to interest rate movement at december wa follows in million pre tax cash flow percentage point instantaneous increase in interest rate one actual prepayment experience could be different than projected quantitative and qualitative disclosure about market risk continued foreign currency risk ford credit policy is to minimize exposure to change in currency exchange rate to meet funding objective ford credit borrows in variety of currency principally dollar canadian dollar euro sterling and renminbi ford credit face exposure to currency exchange rate if mismatch exists between the currency of receivables and the currency of the debt funding those receivables when possible receivables are funded with debt in the same currency minimizing exposure to exchange rate movement when different currency is used ford credit may use foreign currency swap and foreign currency forward to convert substantially all of it foreign currency debt obligation to the local country currency of the receivables result of this policy ford credit belief it market risk exposure relating to change in currency exchange rate at december is insignificant derivative fair value the net fair value of ford credit derivative financial instrument at december wa liability of billion compared to an asset of million at december the decline in net fair value wa driven by higher interest rate and stronger dollar counterparty riskcounterparty risk relates to the loss we could incur if an obligor or counterparty defaulted on an investment or derivative contract we enter into master agreement with counterparties that allow netting of certain exposure in order to manage this risk exposure primarily relate to investment in fixed income instrument and derivative contract used for managing interest rate foreign currency exchange rate and commodity price risk we together with ford credit establish exposure limit for each counterparty to minimize risk and provide counterparty diversification our approach to managing counterparty risk is forward looking and proactive allowing to take risk mitigation action before risk become loss exposure limit are established based on our overall risk tolerance which is calculated from counterparty credit rating and market based credit default swap cd spread the exposure limit are lower for smaller and lower rated counterparties counterparties that have relatively higher cd spread and for longer dated exposure our exposure are monitored on regular basis and included in periodic report to our treasurer substantially all of our counterparty exposure are with counterparties that have an investment grade rating investment grade is our guideline for minimum counterparty long term rating principle generally accepted in the united state of america also in our opinion the company maintained in all material respect effective internal control over financial reporting of december based on item our responsibility is to express opinion on the company consolidated financial statement and on the company internal control over financial reporting based on our audit we are public accounting financial reporting wa maintained in all material respect our audit of the consolidated financial statement included performing procedure to ass the risk of material misstatement of the consolidated material weakness exists and testing and evaluating the design and operating effectiveness of internal control based on the assessed risk our audit also included performing such other procedure we considered necessary in the circumstance we believe that our audit provide reasonable basis for our opinion and limitation of internal control over financial reportinga company internal control over financial reporting is process designed to provide reasonable assurance regarding the reliability of financial reporting and the preparation of financial statement for external purpose in accordance with generally accepted accounting principle company internal control over financial reporting includes those policy and procedure that pertain to the maintenance of record that in reasonable detail accurately and fairly reflect the transaction and disposition of the asset of the company ii provide reasonable assurance that transaction are recorded necessary to permit preparation of financial statement in accordance with generally accepted accounting principle and that receipt and expenditure of the company are being made only in accordance with authorization of management and director of the company and iii provide reasonable assurance regarding prevention or timely detection of unauthorized acquisition use or disposition of the company asset that could have material effect on the financial statement because of it inherent limitation internal control over financial reporting may not prevent or detect misstatement also projection of any evaluation of effectiveness to future period are subject to the risk that control may become inadequate because of change in condition or that the degree of compliance with the policy or procedure may deteriorate critical audit mattersthe critical audit matter communicated below are matter arising from the current period audit of the consolidated financial statement that were communicated or required to be communicated to the audit committee and that relate to account or disclosure that are material to the consolidated financial statement and ii involved our especially challenging subjective or complex judgment the communication of critical audit matter doe not alter in any way our opinion on the consolidated financial statement taken whole and we are not by communicating the critical audit matter below providing separate securitiesinvestments in debt security with maturity date greater than three month at the date of purchase and other debt security for which there is more than an insignificant risk of change in value due to interest rate quoted price or penalty on withdrawal are classified and accounted for either trading or available for sale marketable security equity security with readily determinable fair value are classified and accounted for trading marketable security realized gain and loss interest income and dividend income on all of our marketable security and unrealized gain and loss on security not classified available for sale are recorded in other income loss net unrealized gain and loss on available for sale security are recognized in unrealized gain and loss on security component of other comprehensive income loss net of tax realized gain and loss and reclassification of accumulated other comprehensive income into net income are measured using the specific identification method on quarterly basis we review our available for sale debt security for credit loss we compare the present value of cash flow expected to be collected from the security with the amortized cost basis of the security if the present value of cash flow expected to be collected is le than the amortized cost basis of the security we determine if credit loss allowance is necessary if credit loss allowance is necessary we will record an allowance limited by the amount that fair value is le than the amortized cost basis and recognize the corresponding charge in other income loss net factor we consider include the severity of the impairment the reason for the decline in value interest rate change and counterparty long term rating trade note and other receivablestrade note and other receivables consist primarily of receivables from contract with customer for the sale of vehicle part and accessory the current portion of trade and note receivables is reported in trade and other receivables net the non current portion of note receivables is reported in other asset trade and note receivables are initially recorded at transaction cost trade receivables are typically outstanding for day or le each reporting period we evaluate the collectibility of the trade and note receivables and record an allowance for credit loss representing our estimate of the expected loss that result from all possible default event over the expected life of the receivables addition to the allowance for credit loss are made by recording charge to bad debt expense reported in selling administrative and other expense and cost of sale trade and note receivables are written off against the allowance for credit loss when the account is deemed to be uncollectible net intangible asset and goodwillindefinite lived intangible asset and goodwill are not amortized but are tested for impairment annually or more frequently if event or circumstance indicate the asset may be impaired goodwill impairment testing is also performed following an allocation of goodwill to business to be disposed or change in reporting unit we test for impairment by assessing qualitative factor to determine whether it is more likely than not that the fair value of the indefinite lived intangible asset or the reporting unit allocated the goodwill is le than it carrying amount if the qualitative assessment indicates possible impairment the carrying value of the asset or reporting unit is compared with it fair value fair value is measured relying primarily on the income approach by applying discounted cash flow method the market approach using market value or multiple and or third party valuation we capitalize and amortize our finite lived intangible asset over their estimated useful life the carrying amount of intangible asset and goodwill is reported in other asset in the non current asset section of our consolidated balance sheet intangible asset are comprised primarily of advertising agreement land right and technology license the net carrying amount of our intangible asset wa million and million at december and respectively for the period presented we have not recorded any material impairment for not recorded any impairment for goodwill motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote summary of significant accounting policy continued held and used long lived asset impairmentwe test long lived asset group when change in circumstance indicate the carrying value may not be recoverable event that trigger test for recoverability include material adverse change in projected revenue or expense present cash flow loss combined with history of cash flow loss and forecast that demonstrates significant continuing loss significant negative industry or economic trend current expectation that long lived asset group will be disposed of significantly before the end of it useful life significant adverse change in the manner in which an asset group is used or in it physical condition or when there is change in the asset grouping in addition investing in new emerging product ev or service connectivity may require substantial upfront investment which may result in initial forecasted negative cash flow in the near term in these instance near term negative cash flow on their own may not be indicative of triggering event for evaluation of impairment in such circumstance we also conduct qualitative evaluation of the business growth trajectory which includes updating our assessment of when positive cash flow are expected to be generated confirming whether established milestone are being achieved and assessing our ability and intent to continue to access required funding to execute the plan if this evaluation indicates triggering event ha occurred test for recoverability is performed when triggering event occurs test for recoverability is performed comparing projected undiscounted future cash flow to the carrying value of the asset group if the undiscounted forecasted cash flow are le than the carrying value of the asset the asset group fair value is measured relying primarily on discounted cash flow method to the extent available we will also consider third party valuation of our long lived asset that were prepared for other business purpose an impairment charge is recognized for the amount by which the carrying value of the asset group exceeds it estimated fair value when an impairment loss is recognized for asset to be held and used the adjusted carrying amount of those asset are depreciated over their remaining useful life for the period presented we have not recorded any material impairment held for sale asset impairmentwe perform an impairment test on disposal group to be discontinued held for sale hf or otherwise disposed when we have committed to an action and the action is expected to be completed within one year we estimate fair value to approximate the expected proceeds to be received le cost to sell and compare it to the carrying value of the disposal group an impairment charge is recognized when the carrying value exceeds the estimated fair value see note we also ass fair value if circumstance arise that were considered unlikely and result we decide not to sell disposal group previously classified hf upon reclassification held and used when there is change to plan of sale and the asset are reclassified from hf to held and used the long lived asset would be reported at the lower of the carrying amount before hf designation adjusted for depreciation that would have been recognized if the asset had not been classified hf or ii the fair value at the date the asset no longer satisfy the criterion for classification hf fair value measurementswe measure fair value of our financial instrument including those held within our pension plan using various valuation method and prioritize the use of observable input the use of observable and unobservable input and their significance in measuring fair value are reflected in our fair value hierarchy level input include quoted price for identical instrument and are the most observable level input include quoted price for similar instrument and observable input such interest rate currency exchange rate and yield curve level input include data not observable in the market and reflect management judgment about the assumption market participant would use in pricing the instrumentsfixed income security equity commingled fund derivative financial instrument and alternative asset are remeasured and presented within our consolidated financial statement at fair value on recurring basis finance receivables and debt are measured at fair value for the purpose of disclosure other asset and liability are measured at fair value on nonrecurring basis transfer into and transfer out of the hierarchy level are recognized if they had taken place at the end of the reporting period motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote summary of significant accounting policy continued valuation methodfixed income security fixed income security primarily include government security government agency security corporate bond and asset backed security we generally measure fair value using price obtained from pricing service or quote from dealer that make market in such security pricing method and input to valuation model used by the pricing service depend on the security type asset class where possible fair value are generated using market input including quoted price the closing price in an exchange market bid price the price at which buyer stand ready to purchase and other market information for fixed income security that are not actively traded the pricing service use alternative method to determine fair value for the security including quote for similar fixed income security matrix pricing discounted cash flow using benchmark curve or other factor in certain case when market data are not available we may use broker quote or pricing service that use proprietary pricing model to determine fair value the proprietary model incorporate unobservable input primarily consisting of prepayment curve discount rate default assumption recovery rate yield assumption and credit spread assumption an annual review is performed on the security price received from our pricing service which includes discussion and analysis of the input used by the pricing service to value our security we also compare the price of certain security sold close to the quarter end to the price of the same security at the balance sheet date to ensure the reported fair value is reasonable equity equity security are primarily exchange traded and are valued based on the closing bid official close or last trade pricing on an active exchange if closing price are not available security are valued at the last quoted bid price or may be valued using the last available price security that are thinly traded or delisted are valued using unobservable pricing data commingled fund fixed income and public equity security may each be combined into commingled fund investment most commingled fund are valued to reflect our interest in the fund based on the reported year end net asset value nav derivative financial instrument exchange traded derivative for which market quotation are readily available are valued at the last reported sale price or official closing price reported by an independent pricing service on the primary market or exchange on which they are traded over the counter derivative are not exchange traded and are valued using independent pricing service or industry standard valuation model such discounted cash flow when discounted cash flow model are used projected future cash flow are discounted to present value using market based expectation for interest rate foreign exchange rate commodity price and the contractual term of the derivative instrument the discount rate used is the relevant benchmark interest rate libor sofr sonia plus an adjustment for non performance risk the adjustment reflects the full credit default swap cd spread applied to net exposure by counterparty considering the master netting agreement and any posted collateral we use our counterparty cd spread when we are in net asset position and our own cd spread when we are in net liability position in case when market data are not available we use broker quote and model black scholes to determine fair value this includes situation where there is lack of liquidity for approximately of dealer financing finance receivables are recorded at the time of origination or purchase at fair value and are subsequently reported at amortized cost net of any allowance for credit loss for all finance receivables ford credit defines past due any payment including principal and interest that is at least day past the contractual due date finance receivables classificationfinance receivables are accounted for held for investment hfi if ford credit ha the intent and ability to hold the receivables for the foreseeable future or until maturity or payoff the determination of intent and ability to hold for the foreseeable future is highly judgmental and requires ford credit to make good faith estimate based on all information available at the time of origination or purchase if ford credit doe not have the intent and ability to hold the receivables then the receivables are classified hf each quarter ford credit make determination of whether it is probable that finance receivables originated or purchased during the quarter will be held for the foreseeable future based on historical receivables sale experience internal forecast and budget well other relevant reliable information available through the date of evaluation for purpose of this determination probable mean at least likely and consistent with the budgeting and forecasting period the foreseeable future mean twelve month ford credit classifies receivables hfi or hf on receivable by receivable basis specific receivables included in off balance sheet sale transaction are generally not identified until the month in which the sale occurs held for investment finance receivables classified hfi are recorded at the time of origination or purchase at fair value and are subsequently reported at amortized cost net of any allowance for credit loss cash flow from finance receivables excluding wholesale and other receivables that were originally classified hfi are recorded an investing activity since gaap requires the statement of cash flow presentation to be based on the original classification of the receivables cash flow from wholesale and other receivables are recorded an operating activity held for sale finance receivables classified hf are carried at the lower of cost or fair value cash flow resulting from the origination or purchase and sale of hf receivables are recorded an operating activity in decrease increase in finance receivables wholesale and other decision ha been made to sell receivables that were originally classified hfi the receivables are reclassified hf and carried at the lower of cost or fair value the valuation adjustment if applicable is recorded in other income loss net to recognize the receivables at the lower of cost or fair value motor company and qualityconsumer portfoliowhen originating consumer receivables ford credit us proprietary scoring system that measure credit quality using information in the credit application proposed contract term credit bureau data and other information after proprietary risk score is generated ford credit decides whether to originate contract using decision process based on judgmental evaluation of the applicant the credit application the proposed contract term credit bureau information fico score proprietary risk score and other information the evaluation emphasizes the applicant ability to pay and customer payment activity each customer develops payment history an internally developed behavioral scoring model is used to assist in determining the best collection strategy which allows ford credit from this scoring model contract are categorized by collection risk ford credit collection model evaluate several factor including origination characteristic updated credit bureau data and payment credit lossesthe allowance for credit loss represents an estimate of the lifetime expected credit loss inherent in finance receivables of the balance sheet date the adequacy of the allowance for credit loss is assessed quarterly adjustment to the allowance for credit loss are made by recording charge to ford credit interest operating and other expense on our consolidated income statement the uncollectible portion of finance receivable is charged to the allowance for credit loss at the earlier of when an account is deemed to be uncollectible or when an account is day delinquent taking into consideration the financial condition of the customer or borrower the value of the collateral recourse to guarantor and other factor charge offs on finance receivables include uncollected amount related to principal interest late fee and other allowable charge recovery on finance receivables previously charged off uncollectible are credited to the allowance for credit loss in the event ford credit repossesses the collateral the receivable is charged off and the collateral is recorded at it estimated fair value le cost to sell and reported in other asset on our consolidated balance sheet consumer portfoliofor consumer receivables that share similar risk characteristic such product type initial credit risk term vintage geography and other relevant factor ford credit estimate the lifetime expected credit loss allowance based on collective assessment using measurement model and management judgment the lifetime expected credit loss for the receivables is determined by applying probability of default and loss given default assumption to monthly expected exposure then discounting these cash flow to present value using the receivable original effective interest rate or the current effective interest rate for variable rate receivable probability of default model are developed from internal risk scoring model taking into account the expected probability of payment and time to default adjusted for macroeconomic outlook and recent performance the model consider factor such risk evaluation at the time of origination historical trend in credit loss which include the impact of tdrs and the composition and recent performance of the present portfolio including vehicle brand term risk evaluation and new used vehicle the loss given default is the percentage of the expected balance due at default that is not recoverable taking into account the expected collateral value and trend in recovery including key metric such delinquency repossession and bankruptcy monthly exposure are equal to the receivables expected outstanding principal and interest balance the allowance for credit loss incorporates forward looking macroeconomic condition for baseline upturn and downturn scenario three separate credit loss allowance are calculated from these scenario they are then probability weighted to determine the quantitative estimate of the credit loss allowance recognized in the financial statement ford credit us forecast from third party that revert to long term historical average after reasonable and supportable forecasting period which is specific to the particular macroeconomic variable and which varies by market ford credit update the forward looking macroeconomic forecast quarterly if management doe not believe the model reflect lifetime expected credit loss for the portfolio an adjustment is made to reflect management judgment regarding qualitative factor including economic uncertainty observable change in portfolio performance and other relevant factor on an ongoing basis ford credit review it model including macroeconomic factor the selection of macroeconomic scenario and their weighting to ensure they reflect the risk of the portfolio motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote ford credit finance receivables and allowance for credit loss continued non consumer portfoliodealer financing is evaluated on an individual dealer basis by segmenting dealer by risk characteristic such the amount of the loan the nature of the collateral the financial status of the dealer and any tdr modification to determine if an individual dealer requires specific allowance for credit loss if required the allowance is based on the present value of the expected future cash flow of the dealer receivables discounted at the loan original effective interest rate or the fair value of the collateral adjusted for estimated cost to sell for the remaining dealer financing ford credit estimate an allowance for credit loss on collective basis wholesale loan ford credit estimate the allowance for credit loss for wholesale loan based on historical loss to receivable ltr ratio expected future cash flow and the fair value of collateral for wholesale loan with similar risk characteristic the allowance for credit loss is estimated on collective basis using the ltr model and management judgment the ltr model is based on the most recent year of history an ltr ratio is calculated by dividing credit loss charge offs net of recovery by average net finance receivables excluding unearned interest supplement and allowance for credit loss the average ltr ratio is multiplied by the end of period balance representing the lifetime expected credit loss reserve dealer loan ford credit us weighted average remaining maturity method to estimate the lifetime expected credit loss reserve for dealer loan the loss model is based on the industry wide commercial real estate credit loss adjusted to factor in the historical credit loss for the dealer loan portfolio the expected credit loss is calculated under different macroeconomic scenario that are weighted to provide the total lifetime expected credit loss after establishing the collective and specific allowance for credit loss if management belief the allowance doe not reflect all loss inherent in the portfolio due to change in recent economic trend and condition or other relevant forward looking economic factor an adjustment is made based on management judgment motor company and subsidiariesnotes to the financial statementsnote ford credit manager to use efficient substitute for traditional security and to manage exposure to interest rate and foreign exchange risk interest rate and foreign currency derivative instrument are used for the purpose of hedging change in the fair value of asset that result from interest rate change and currency fluctuation interest rate derivative are also used to adjust portfolio duration derivative may not be used to leverage or to alter the economic exposure to an asset class outside the scope of the mandate an investment manager ha been given alternative investment manager are permitted to employ leverage including through the use of derivative or other tool that may alter economic exposure alternative investment execute diverse strategy that provide exposure to broad range of hedge fund strategy equity investment in private company and investment in private property fund significant concentration of risk significant concentration of risk in our plan asset relate to interest rate growth asset and operating risk in order to minimize asset volatility relative to the obligation the majority of plan asset are allocated to fixed income investment which are exposed to interest rate risk rate increase generally will result in decline in the value of fixed income asset while reducing the present value of the obligation conversely rate decrease generally will increase the value of fixed income asset offsetting the related increase in the obligation in order to ensure asset are sufficient to pay benefit portion of plan asset is allocated to growth asset primarily hedge fund real estate private equity and public equity that are expected over time to earn higher return with more volatility than fixed income investment which more closely match pension obligation within growth asset risk is mitigated by constructing portfolio that is broadly diversified by asset class investment strategy manager style and process operating risk include the risk of inadequate diversification and weak control to mitigate these risk investment are diversified across and within asset class in support of investment objective policy and practice to address operating risk include ongoing
